Link: "Diagnosis of acute pulmonary embolism" on UpToDate.


Patient Presentation: Respiratory Difficulties
Physician Tasks/ Skills: Diagnostic Technologies
Body System: Respiratory System
Discipline: Emergency Medicine
A 36-year-old female presents to the emergency department with the complaints of shortness of breath and palpitations. History reveals the symptoms began three hours ago. She recently returned home from a twelve-hour flight. Past medical history is noncontributory and the only medications she admits to taking daily are oral contraceptive pills. She admits to a recent tobacco use that began six months ago. Vitals reveals a blood pressure of 120/70 mmHg, a heart rate of 108/min, and temperature of 100.4ºF. The most accurate diagnostic step is

1. chest radiograph
2. echocardiogram
3. lower extremity ultrasound
4. non-contrast chest CT
5. pulmonary angiography

The correct answer is: E
This case has a high clinical suspicion of a pulmonary embolism (PE). Risk factors include the patient's age above 35 years, oral contraceptive use, tobacco use, and recent travel. The best imaging studies to diagnose pulmonary embolism are pulmonary angiography or a contrast-enhanced CT angiography. CT angiography is the initial imaging modality of choice for stable patients with suspected pulmonary embolism, but is not a choice in the above scenario. Pulmonary angiography is the test of choice with CT angiography is not available.

Answer A: Chest radiographs are abnormal in most cases of pulmonary embolism, but the findings are nonspecific. Common radiographic abnormalities include atelectasis, pleural effusion, parenchymal opacities, and elevation of a hemidiaphragm. The classic radiographic findings of pulmonary infarction include a wedge-shaped, pleura-based triangular opacity with an apex pointing toward the hilus (Hampton hump) or decreased vascularity (Westermark sign). These findings are suggestive of pulmonary embolism but are infrequently observed.


Answer B: Echocardiogram is rarely done to diagnose PE. Findings include tricuspid regurgitation, increased right ventricular size and decreased right ventricular function. Positive findings on echocardiogram are found in about 30-40% of patients with PE.


Answer C: Lower extremity Doppler to look for a DVT is appropriate if CT angiography or pulmonary angiography are not available and the V/Q scan is inconclusive for a patient with high clinical probability. The diagnosis of pulmonary embolism can be proven by demonstrating the presence of a DVT at any site. This may sometimes be accomplished noninvasively by using duplex ultrasonography. A negative ultrasonographic scan does not rule out DVT, because many DVTs occur in areas that are inaccessible to ultrasonographic examination.


Answer D: A non-contrast CT plays no role. Contrast is needed to detect the embolism within the blood vessel.




Bottom Line: A pulmonary angiogram or contrast enhanced chest CT is the next best step in management for stable patients with a high clinical suspicion PE.

For more information, see:
"Diagnosis of acute pulmonary embolism" on UpToDate.
"Pulmonary Embolism Workup" on Medscape.

Patient Presentation: Pregnancy/Childbirth/Postpartum/Neonatal Assessment
Physician Tasks/ Skills: Diagnostic Technologies
Body System: Asymptomatic & General Symptoms
Discipline: Obstetrics/Gynecology
A 28-year-old female, gravida two, para one, presents to the office with the complaint of decreased fetal movement. A biophysical profile is performed. Within 30 minutes, the fetus is noted to have one discrete body movement, one opening and closing of the hand, an episode of breathing lasting 10 seconds, an amniotic fluid pocket of 4 centimeters, and a non-reactive non-stress test. The biophysical profile score for this fetus is

1. two
2. three
3. four
4. five
5. six

The correct answer is: C
Biophysical profiles are a means of antepartum testing that can be utilized to prevent fetal death. Scoring is based on five components: breathing, gross body movement, fetal tone, reactive non-stress test, and amniotic fluid volume. Normal testing awards a score of 2, while abnormal testing awards a score of 0. Therefore, all testing results will be an even number. Total maximum score is 10 and testing occurs within a thirty minute time period. Two points are awarded for breathing if there is at least one episode of 30 seconds of breathing. Gross body movement is normal if there are at least 3 discrete body/limb movements. Fetal tone is normal if there is at least 1 episode of extension of extremity and return to flexion, or opening or closing of the hand. At least two accelerations must be present for a reactive non-stress test. Amniotic fluid analysis must have at least 1 pocket of amniotic fluid >2cm. The above case would be awarded points for fetal tone and amniotic fluid, giving a final score of 4/10.

Answers A & E: The above case would be awarded points for fetal tone and amniotic fluid, giving a final score of 4/10.


Answers B & D: Biophysical profile scoring is always reported in even numbers.




Bottom Line: Biophysical profile scoring is based on breathing, gross body movement, fetal tone, reactive non-stress test, and amniotic fluid volume.

For more information, see:
"Ultrasonography in biophysical profile" on Medscape.
